Jamison Brereton

139
All Gods
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
11 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi, except br╠еhat─л 5, triс╣гс╣нubh 11
This complex hymn presents many interpretational difficulties, though it roughly follows the model of the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra, a recitation at the Morning Pressing found also in R╠еgveda I.2тАУ3, I.23, and II.41. The order of divinities in the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra is V─Бyu, Indra and V─Бyu, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, the A┼Ыvins, Indra, the All Gods, and Sarasvat─л; this hymn follows this order through verse 6: Indra and V─Бyu (vs. 1), Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (vs. 2), the A┼Ыvins (vss. 3тАУ5), Indra (vs. 6), but ends with Agni (vs. 7), the Maruts (vs. 8), Indra and Agni (vs. 9), and Br╠еhaspati (vs. 10), with verse 11 in a different meter and addressed to all the gods collectively.
The ritual situation is established at the very beginning, with the quotation of a familiar sacrificial formula ├бstu ┼Ыrauс╣гaс╣н, found all over middle Vedic ritual texts. This ritual-internal quotation is matched, in ring-compositional style, by the quotation of a praiс╣гa, or ritual command to the Hotar, in verse 10, the last real verse of the hymn. It is also clear that the time is early morning (see esp. vs. 4, though there are also more oblique indications in the first two verses), and that the sound of the pressing stones is calling the gods to the sacrifice (see vs. 3, and its ring-compositional echo in vs. 10).
As so often, the difficulties in the hymn may stem in part from the fact that the poet is reflecting on his poetic lineage and calling. The obscure reference to the тАЬumbilical tieтАЭ or тАЬnavelтАЭ in verse 1 is made somewhat clearer by verse 9, in which the poet asserts that his тАЬumbilical tiesтАЭ are with a series of earlier seers and sacri
ficers, including ManuтАФwhose own ties are to the gods. He thus provides himself with a poetic pedigree and in following their track, or model, produces his own hymns that have some chance of reaching the gods, since his predecessorsтАЩ did. In verse 1 he mentions only one such predecessor: Vivasvant (lit., тАЬpossessing the shining forthтАЭ), who in later Vedic and even in late R╠еgveda (V─Бlakh., VIII.52.1) is considered the father of Manu and who is often associated, as a proto-priest, with the pressing of soma. (His Avestan correspondent V─лva┼Лuuaс╣Зt is the first man who pressed haoma [Y 9.4].) So in verse 1 our poet proclaims that he is beginning a new hymn, by newly attaching himself to a legendary seer-sacrificer. But there is another likely meaning there as well: Vivasvant is identified as the sun in later Vedic, and quite possibly in some passages in the R╠еgveda as well, and therefore the poet may also be making reference to the time of тАЬshining forth,тАЭ namely early morning.
The double reference to ritual poetry and to dawn continues in verse 2. Mitra and Varuс╣Зa take тАЬuntruth away from truth,тАЭ thus enabling the poet and his peers to see the godsтАЩ golden throne. On the one hand, the untruth can be darkness, and the removal of this darkness reveals the sun. On the other hand, the priests see this vision with their insights and their mind, and though they also see with their eyes, these are the тАЬeyes of soma,тАЭ presumably the vision arising from drinking the soma. So on another level of interpretation what they see is a poetic vision.
The three A┼Ыvins verses (3тАУ5) are fairly clear descriptions of the journey of those gods to the dawn sacrifice, and the invitation to Indra (vs. 6) is also straightforward, as is the praise of the Maruts (vs. 8). This clarity is unfortunately obscured in verse 7, whose translation is only provisional, though the direct speech of Agni is quite intriguing. He seems to be chiding the gods for having given the Aс╣Еgirases a cow they (or in most interpretations, Aryaman and unspecified others) have milked out. From the mythological point of view, the cow should represent the cows imprisoned in the Vala cave that the Aс╣Еgirases helped to liberate. In a ritual context this could be the cow that provides the milk to mix with soma; in a poetic context the poetic insight or vision that provided the Aс╣Еgirases with songs. The role of Aryaman here is entirely unclear.
As noted above, in verse 9 the poet situates himself in the poetic and sacrificial tradition, and in verse 10, another obscure verse (Geldner calls it тАЬunintelligibleтАЭ [unversta╠Иndlich]), the ritual and poetic ring is closed.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay our prayers be heard, I plural ce before (me) Agni with reverence; we have recourse to his celestial might; we have recourse to Indra and to V─Бyu; which doing, a new (hymn) has been addressed (by us) to the radiant navel (of the earth); and thereupon may our pious rites attain the gods; may our pious rites attain the presence of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Astu srauс╣гat = asy─Бс╕е stuter ┼Ыravaс╣Зam bhavatu, may there be a hearing of this hymn, or ┼Ыrot─Б bhavatu = may Agni or other deity be a hearer. ┼Ыrauс╣гat. is an exclamation uttered when the butter is poured upon the fire, on the altar, as an offering to the gods. The radiant navel of the earth: may refer to the altar or the sacrifice; yaj├▒am ─Бhur bhuvanasya n─Бbhim (yajam─Бhurbhuvanasya n─Бbhim–Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 7.4.17.2), they have called the sacrifice the navel of the world; the text adds vivasvati = d─лptimat, shining; Vivasvat may also refer to the Sun-god

Jamison Brereton

(Cry) тАЬLet it be; he will hear.тАЭ I place Agni in front through my insight. Now we choose that heavenly troopтАФwe choose Indra and V─Бyu.
Since our (umbilical tie) has been effectively bound anew to the umbilical tie in VivasvantтАЩs (sphere),
then let our thoughts go forthтАФour thoughts (going) as if to the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pass. aor. saс╣Гd─Б╠Бyi is taken by Grassmann (etc.) to тИЪd─Б тАШtieтАЩ, surely correctly.

But there are several other occurrences of this lexeme s├бm тИЪd─Б that also appear to express the same idiom, but, with different morphological realizations, are generally assigned to тИЪd─Б тАШgiveтАЩ (though see, e.g., K├╝mmel 244). The idiom, in its fullest expression, is s├бm тИЪd─Б n─Б╠Бbhim [ACC] n─Б╠Бbh─Б(u) [LOC] тАШtie navel to navelтАЩ, that is, to assert a family connection (often between gods or semidivine figures like seers and us humans. In the passive the first navel is of course in the nom. - a nom. that is gapped in this passage. Another ex. of the idiom is found in IV.44.5, also passive, this time with the loc. gapped (or substituted for by a prn.): s├бс╣Г y├бd dad├й n─Б╠Бbhiс╕е p┼лrvy─Б╠Бv─Бm тАЬbecause (our) ancient umbilical tie is attached to you (or, to your [navel]),тАЭ of the A┼Ыvins. Instead of s├бm the preverb can be ─Б╠Б: see IX.10.8 with the fullest form of the idiom, containing both case forms of тАШnavelтАЩ: n─Б╠Бbh─Б n─Б╠Бbhiс╣Г na ─Б╠Бdade тАЬhe has bound his navel to our navel.тАЭ Also IX.79.4 div├н te n─Б╠Бbh─Б param├│ y├б ─Бdad├й тАЬIt was in heaven, to its navel, that your highest (navel) was bound.тАЭ (This last tr. is different from the published one; see comm. ad IX.79.4 for the alteration and the difficulties in the passage.) Another ex. of the idiom is probably found in the noun saс╣Гdad├н- in IX.99.7, though the telltale navel is absent. See disc. there. The other occurrence of saс╣Гdad├нin II.39.7 even more attenuated, but still expresses the sense of attachment. A variant of the idiom, ─Б╠БтИЪtan n─Б╠Бbhim LOC is found in I.105.9; see comm. there.

Griffith

HEARD be our prayer! In thought I honour Agni first: now straightway we elect this heavenly company, Indra and Vayu we elect.
For when our latest thought is raised and on Vivasvan centred well,
Then may our holy songs go forward on their way, our songs as ’twere unto the Gods.

Geldner

Alles lausche! Mit Bedacht stelle ich Agni an die Spitze. Wir erk├╝ren jetzt die himmlische Heerschar, Indra und Varuna erk├╝ren wir uns. Wenn die bei Vivasvat geschlossene Verwandtschaft aufs neue an unsere Verwandtschaft angekn├╝pft wird, dann sollen fein unsere frommen Gedanken zu ihnen gehen, wie sich┬┤s zu den G├╢ttern ziemt, die frommen Gedanken.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa, bestow (upon us) abundantly that unenduring water which you obtain from the sun, through your own energy; through the inherent energy of the vigorous; may we thus behold your golden (forms) in our halls of sacrifice, (brought thither) by our sacred rites, and by our thoughts and senses (intent upon you); by our senses (intent upon offering) the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Since, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, you took untruth away from truth by your own fervorтАФby your own fervor of skillтАФ
just in this way among the seats we saw the golden (throne) of you two, just with our insights and with our mind, with our own eyesтАФwith our own eyes of soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner (etc.) I supply тАШthroneтАЩ with hiraс╣Зy├бyam in e on the basis of V.62.8.

01-02 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

For the sense of these vss., see published introduction.

Griffith

As there ye, Mitra, Varuna, above the true have taken to yourselves the untrue with your mind, with wisdom’s mental energy,
So in the seats wherein ye dwell have we beheld the Golden One,
Not with our thoughts or spirit, but with these our eyes, yea, with the eyes that Soma gives.

Geldner

Als ihr beide, Mitra und Varuna, da vom Rechten das Unrechte wegnahmet mit eurem Eifer, mit dem eurer Willenskraft eignen Eifer, da sahen wir dort an euren Sitzen, den goldenen Stuhl, wenn auch nur im Gedanken, im Geiste, mit eigenen Augen, durch die eigenen Augen des Soma.

Grassmann

Wie ihr ja, Mitra, Varuna, zum Schutz des Rechts das Unrecht packt mit eures eignen Zornes Macht, mit eures Geistes innerm Zorn, So haben wir auf euerm Sitz f├╝rwahr geschaut das goldne Recht, Mit Geist und Sinn, ja mit den eignen Augen auch, mit Soma’s eignen Augen auch.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, men who desire to glorify you with (their) hymns, cause, as it were, their praises to be heard, propitiating you with oblations; for, from you, who are possessed of all opulence, (they obtain) every kind of wealth and abundant food. Dasras, the fellies (of the wheels) of your honey-laden car drop honey, (carried) in your golden (car).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hiraс╣Зyaye rathe dasr─Б hiraс╣Зyaye: the epithet means ‘golden’; the first occurrence is interpreted as madhup┼лrс╣Зa = pruс╣г─Бyante pavayaс╕е (pav─л rathanemirbhavati yadvipun─Бti bh┼лmim–Nirukta 5.5), the circumferences of the wheels distil (kс╣гaranti sravanti), or scatter honey, as they revolve; in the second occurrence, hirс╣Зyaye is explained as ‘plural asing, heart-delighting’, hс╣Ыdayaramaс╣Зa; and to provide an assumed ellipse, by havir-vahatam, ‘convey the oblation in your delightful chariot’

Jamison Brereton

O A┼Ыvins, the ─Аyus, seeking the gods, with their praise songs are causing you two to hear, as if making the signal-call (of the pressing stone)
heardтАФthe ─Аyus (are causing) you two (to hear) about the oblations.

In you two are all splendors and nourishments, o you who grant all possessions.
The wheel-rims on your golden one spray (honey)тАФon your golden chariot, wondrous ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The part. ─Б┼Ыr─Бv├бyanta(с╕е) is best taken as predicated, substituting for a main verb. The standard tr. supply a finite verb (тАЬinviteтАЭ vel sim.), but this seems unnecessary.

This form also participates in a fine example of case disharmony in a simile (in the sense of Jamison 1982): ┼Ыr─Бv├бya-/┼Ыrav├бya- can mean both тАЬcause to be heardтАЭ and тАЬcause to hear.тАЭ In the simile (p─Бda b) it takes ┼Ыl├│kam as obj. and means тАЬcause to be heardтАЭ; in the frame (p─Бda a) it takes yuv─Б╠Бm and means тАЬcause to hear,тАЭ while in the tag-p─Бda (c) it likewise takes yuv─Б╠Бm but also a 2nd acc. havy─Б╠Б, with the meaning тАЬcause X to hear (about) Y.тАЭ With Geldner I supply тАЬof the pressing stoneтАЭ with ┼Ыl├│kam on the basis of 10e ┼Ыl├│kam ├бdreс╕е.

Unlike the standard tr. I supply тАЬchariotтАЭ as the obj. of anu┼Ы─Б╠Бsat─Б and take r├бjaс╕е as an acc. of extent.

Griffith

Asvins, the pious call you with their hymns of praise, sounding their loud song forth to you, these living men, to their oblations, living men.

The fellies of your golden chariot scatter drops, Mighty Ones! of your golden car.

English translation:

тАЬDasras, your purpose is known; you would repair to heaven; your charioteers harness (your steeds) for your heavenward journey; the horses that injure not (the car) on your journey to heaven. We have plural ced you, Dasras, in your golden three-shafted chariot, going by an (easy) road to heaven, humiliators (of enemies), and principal regulators of the rain.тАЭ

A├▒jas─Б ┼Ы─Бsat─Б rajas = udakam, water; vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нi-lakс╣гaс╣Зam, metony for rain

Jamison Brereton

It has appeared, wondrous ones: you two unclose the firmament; your chariot-horses are yoked at the rituals of daybreakтАФthe
unbesmirched ones at the rituals of daybreak.
Your station is on your chariot box, on your golden chariot,
wondrous onesтАФ
(you two) going as if on a path, directing (the chariot) through the dusky realmтАФdirecting (it) straightway through the dusky realm.

Griffith

Well is it known, O Mighty Ones: ye open heaven; for you the chariot-steeds are yoked for morning rites, unswerving steeds for morning rites,
We set you on the chariot-seat, ye Mighty, on the golden car.
Ye seek mid-air as by a path that leads aright, as by a path that leads direct.

Euer Stand ist auf dem Wagensitz, auf dem goldnen Wagen, o Meister. Wie auf der rechten Stra├Яe geht ihr die Richtung weisend durch die Luft, richtig weisend durch die Luft.

Elizarenkova

тАЬEnriched by holy rites, grant us, by day and night, (all good things), on account of our pious acts; never may your donations, never may our (donations), be withheld.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, showerer (of blessings), these effused Soma, (expressed) by stones, and which have sprung (from mountain), are for your drinking; these libations have burst forth for you; may they satisfy you as an offering presented (in the hope of receiving) great and wonderful riches. Acceptor of laudations, come to us, glorified by our hymns; come to us well plural ased.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O bull IndraтАФthese pressed drops, the drink of a bull, pressed by the stones, are bursting outтАФfor you are the pressed (drops) bursting out.
Let them invigorate you to giving, to great, glittering generosity. Being praised with songs, you whose vehicle is songs, come hereтАФvery compassionate to us, come here.

Griffith

These Soma-drops, strong Indra! drink for heroes, poured, pressed out by pressing-stones, are welling forth for thee, for thee the drops are welling forth.
They shall make glad thy heart to give, to give wealth great and wonderful.
Thou who acceptest praise come glorified by hymns, come thou to us benevolent.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, listen attentively when you are praised by us, and repeat (those praises) to the gods who are entitled to worship; to the royal (deities) entitled to worship; on which accoun tthe gods gave to the Aс╣Еgirasas the cow which Aryaman milked for (you), the maker (of all), together with the gods; that cow (the nature of which you have said), he, along with me, comprehends.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cow which Aryaman milked: The legend is tha Aс╣Еgirasas, having propitiated the gods, solicited the gift of a cow; the gods them the cow of plural nty, but they were unable to milk her, and applied to Aryaman, who drew from the cow milk convertible to butter for oblations to fire. eс╣гa t─Бm veda me sac─Б = he knows her along with me; this is explained: aryam─Бham api j─Бn─Бmi, either I, Aryam─Б, or I and Aryam─Б know her

Jamison Brereton

Listen to us, Agni: Reverently invoked, you will say to the gods worthy of the sacrificeтАФto the kings worthy of the sacrifice:
тАЬSince, gods, you have given this milk-cow to the Aс╣Еgirases,
they milk her dry. Aryaman is in partnership with the performer [=Agni/priest]тАФhe knows her (too), in partnership with me
[=Agni].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the difficulties of interpr. of this verse, see published introduction.

In f Geldner and Renou take aryam─Б╠Бas subject of duhre and are then at pains to assemble enough other personnel to count, at least conceptually, as a plural with pl.

verb duhre. (Cf. Renou тАЬAryaman (ainsi que) l’officiant (et autres) l’ont traite-├а-fond.тАЭ) But not only does this not work grammatically but it does not make sense: since the gods gave the cow to the Aс╣Еgirases (de), surely they are the ones who have milked her dry. Although major syntactic breaks in the middle of p─Бdas are rare, in this case we must take sg. aryam─Б╠Бas starting a new sentence (so also Witzel Got┼Н). Note that p─Бda a also seems to have a syntactic break after ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зuhi, though it is less jarring because the subject of the next clause remains the same.

As for the sense, I am quite baffled. The Aс╣Еgirases seem to have mistreated the cow, or at least gotten everything they can out of her. But Aryaman also has knowledge, and perhaps use, of her. I suggest very tentatively that since Aryaman is associated with the householderтАЩs fire and with hospitality rites, this may be an early and oblique reference to a division between what will later be known as ┼Ыrauta rites and gс╣Ыhya rites. But I have no confidence in this.

Griffith

Quickly, O Agni, hear us: magnified by us thou shalt speck for us to the Gods adorable yea, to the Kings adorable:
When, O ye Deities, ye gave that Milch-cow to the Angirases,
They milked her: Aryaman, joined with them, did the work: he knoweth her as well as I.

Geldner

H├╢r uns recht, Agni; du sollst berufen den opferw├╝rdigen G├╢ttern melden, den opferw├╝rdigen K├╢nigen: Seit ihr G├╢tter diese Milchkuh den Angiras┬┤ geschenkt habt, melken diese der reiche Patron in Gemeinschaft mit dem aus├╝benden Priester aus; er wei├Я sie bei mir.

Grassmann

Auch du, o Agni, h├╢r auf uns, gepriesener, du m├╢gest sprechen zu den heil’gen G├╢ttern nun, zu den ehrw├╝rd’gen K├╢nigen: ┬╗Als jene Milchkuh, G├╢tter, ihr den Angiras zum Lohne gabt, Da molken sie und Arjaman beim Priester sie;er kennt die Kuh so gut als ich.┬л

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNever, Maruts, may your glorious energies be exerted against us; may our (riches) never diminish; never may our towns decay; and may whatever is wonderful, admirable immortal, or (whatever is recognized to be living), from its sound, that has been yours from age to age, (devolve) upon us; whatever is most difficult (of attainment) bestow upon us; whatever is most difficult (to be attained).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ghoс╣г─Бt = ghoс╣г─Бс╕е, plural sounds, noises; and by metonymy, those who utter them, either cattle or people

Jamison Brereton

Let these manly deeds of yours not get old because of us, and let the brilliant deeds not ageтАФlet them not age before us.
What glittering, immortal (deed) of yours shall sound anew in every generation,
o Maruts, fix that firm in us as well as (brilliance) difficult to surpassтАФ and what is difficult to surpass.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On asm├бd abh├н see comm. ad V.33.3.

The standard tr. supply тАШwordтАЩ (v├бcaс╕е Geldner n. 8a) as the neut. sg. subject with y├бd тАж citr├бm тАж in de, but a singular form of pa├║с╣Гsya- in ab is more easily supplied from context, and deeds can easily тАЬresoundтАЭ by semantic transference.

I interpr. the structure of d-g differently from the standard interpr., which take t├бd as the antecedent both of the y├бd clause in de (y├бd тАж gh├│с╣г─Бt тАж) and the one in f, y├бc ca duс╣гс╣н├бram, echoed by g. By this interpr. the two y├бd clauses are overtly conjoined (y├бd тАж y├бc ca) around the main clause referent (t├бd), with the 2nd embedded in the main cl. before the verb didhс╣Ыt─Б╠Бin the echo p─Бda. Klein explicitly accounts for this disruption of structure by asserting that the y├бc ca clause тАЬhas been postposed in p─Бda c because its required repetition in d provides a coherent punaс╕еpadamтАЭ [he must mean f and g respectively]. This seems like a bit of a cop out to me - it wouldnтАЩt be тАЬrequiredтАЭ to be repeated if it hadnтАЩt ended up in that position in the first place, for other reasons. Contrary to this analysis, I take f(g) as containing an тАЬX and which YтАЭ (t├бd тАж y├бc ca) construction of the familiar type, with two different referents. The X is also further specified by the preposed rel. cl. in de (y├бd vaс╕е тАж ├бmartyam), but the y├бd clause in de and the one in f (echoed by g) are entirely unconnected and have different referents. The placement of the y├бc ca clause and the ca seem to me strong evidence for my interpretation.

As for the referent of y├бc ca duс╣гс╣н├бram (fg), I supply dyumn├бm also from context (b dyumn─Б╠Бni); cf. also III.37.10 dyumn├бс╣Г dadhiс╣гva duс╣гс╣н├бram.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ancient Dadhya├▒c, Aс╣Еgiras, Priyamedha, Kaс╣Зva, Atri, Manu, have known my birth; they who were of old and Manu have known (my progenitors); for of them is long life amongst the gods, and in them is our existence; for the sake of their nigh station, I adore (the gods) with praise; I worship Indra and Agni with praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

My birth: the birth of me, Parucchepas, the с╣Ыс╣гi of the hymn; he is subsequent to them or of more recent date. te me p┼лrve manur viduс╕е: added is pitr─Бd─лn, fathers;

Manu = manavaс╕е, plural, i.e. former Manus; p┼лrve is applied to those previously named, Dadhya├▒c and the rest; manava┼Ыca and the Manus. In them is our existence: asm─Бkam teс╣гu n─Бbhayaс╕е, in them are our ’navels’; explained as vital airs, in connection with life, j─лvena saha saс╣Гbandhavantaс╕е pr─Бс╣З─Бс╕е; or by sacrifices in relation to their rewards, phalena saс╣Гbaddh─Бс╕е y─Бg─Бс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Dadhya├▒c, the earlier Aс╣Еgiras, Priyamedha, Kaс╣Зva, Atri, and Manu know my birthтАФthese earlier ones and Manu know mine.
Their attachment is to the gods; our umbilical ties are to them
[=ancient seers].
(Following) along their track I bend (them) here greatly with a songтАФI bend Indra and Agni here with a song.

Griffith

Dadhyac of old, Angiras, Priyamedha these, and Kanva, Atri, Manu knew my birth, yea, those of ancient days and Manu knew.
Their long line stretcheth to the Gods, our birth-connexions are with them.
To these, for their high station, I bow down with song, to Indra, Agni, bow with song.

In ihren Fu├Яtapfen ziehe ich mit meiner Lobrede m├дchtig an, ziehe ich mit meiner Lobrede Indra und Agni an.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the invoker (of the gods) offer sacrifice, and may they, desirous of the offering, (partake of) the acceptable (libation); Bс╣Ыhaspati himself, desiring (the libation), celebrates worship with libations; with copious and excellent libations. We catch from a distant quarter the sound of the stones, whereby the performer of pious acts has of himself secured the waters (of the clouds); the performer of pious acts (has secured) many habitations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Atman─Б adh─Бrayad ararind─Бni (ararind─Бni dhvasmanvat–Nirukta 1.12.16= vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нi lakс╣гaс╣З─Бnyudak─Бni atman─Б dharayati, he sustains by himself the waters, that is, the rains; or, he produces such waters by his sacrifices, tadс╣Ы┼Ыaс╣Зyudakam y─Бgena utp─Бdayati, rain being the result of worship. Pious acts: sakratuс╕е = yajam─Бna or Bс╣Ыhaspati, as the adhvaryu, or ministering priest

Jamison Brereton

(Crying) тАЬThe Hotar-priest shall sacrifice,тАЭ he wins what is choice of the wooden (cup) [=soma]. Br╠еhaspati the seeker sacrifices with the bulls [=soma drinks?]тАФwith the bulls with their many choice gifts.
By ourselves we have grasped the signal-call of the pressing-stone signaling its intentions afar. The very resolute one upheld the fittings [?]тАФthe very resolute one
(upheld) the many seats.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The praiс╣гa quoted at the beginning of this verse, matching the one opening the hymn, situates this verse in the ritual here and now, and such a context gives clues for the solution of some of the difficulties. Because the context is the soma sacrifice (the pra├╝ga┼Ыastra is part of the morning soma pressing; see also the pressing stone in e), I follow Geldner in taking van├нnaс╕е as the gen. sg. of тАШwoodenтАЩ (rather than as the nom. pl. of a putative van├нn- тАШwinningтАЩ, with Renou). The тАШwoodenтАЩ is the wooden cup and by extension its contents: soma. This interpr. in turn makes it unnec. to take vanta as a haplology of 3rd pl. *vananta (see Oldenberg). The bulls of b are likewise interpretable in a ritual context as the soma drinks.

P─Бda f contains an incomprehensible hapax arar├нnd─Бni, which, as so often, may have been stimulated by the phonological context: ├бdh─Бrayadararind─Бni. Given the construction of the tag-p─Бda g it should refer to something compatible with s├бdm─Бni тАШseatsтАЩ. My тАШfittingsтАЩ is only a placeholder, loosely implying a connection with тИЪс╣Ы тАШfit togetherтАЩ (also in ar├б- тАШwheel-spokeтАЩ, etc.) and inspired by the (presumably entirely accidental) echo of с╝А╧Б╬▒╧Бс╜╖╧Г╬║╧Й. What -ind- would be under this analysis is utterly unclear.

English translation:

тАЬGods who are eleven in heaven; who are eleven on earth; and who are eleven dwelling with glory in mid-air; may you be plural ased with our sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tisraс╕е eva devat─Бс╕е (Nirukta 7.5)

Jamison Brereton

O gods, the eleven of you who are in heaven, the eleven who are on the earth,
the eleven who dwell in the waters in their greatnessтАФ(all) of you, gods, take pleasure in this sacrifice here.
Hymns I.140тАУ164 are attributed to D─лrghatamas, the son of Ucatha, who calls himself M─Бmateya, the son of Mamat─Б, in I.147.3, 152.6, and 158.6. The name D─лrghatamas means the one тАЬof long darkness.тАЭ The Br╠еhaddevat─Б IV.14тАУ15 (Macdonell) explains that he received this name because he was born blind, and the poet himself refers to his blindness in I.147.3. According to the Br╠еhaddevat─Б his sight was later restored by the gods. His name is also an appropriate reflection of the difficulty of many of his hymns. His affection for word play, symbolic language, syntactic anomaly, and ambiguous reference makes his hymns distinctive, original, and often highly elusive. He is one of the most challenging, but at the same time one of the most interesting poets of the R╠еgveda.
His hymns also present an unusual sequence of divinities. The list begins con ventionally enough with I.140тАУ150, which are dedicated to Agni, but the ordinar ily expected series to Indra is missing. Instead 151тАУ153 are to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, 154тАУ156 to Viс╣гс╣Зu or to Viс╣гс╣Зu and Indra, 157тАУ158 to the A┼Ыvins, 159тАУ160 to Heaven and Earth, and 161 to the R╠еbhus. Then 162 and 163 are praises of the sacrificial horse, and 164, the climax of the collection, is a very long and very puzzling riddle hymn, which explores the mysteries of several Vedic rites. The second A┼Ыvin hymn, I.158, is of particular interest because it is ostensibly an autobiographical hymn, composed when the poet was an old man and on the verge of being pushed aside. Partly on the basis of this hymn Br╠еhaddevat─Б IV.21тАУ25 gives a second legend that his servants tried to drown D─лrghatamas. But he floated downstream and was res cued in Aс╣Еga where he married and then gave birth to the poet Kakс╣г─лvant.

Griffith

O ye Eleven Gods whose home is heaven, O ye Eleven who make earth your dwelling,
Ye who with might, Eleven, live in waters, accept this sacrifice, O Gods, with pleasure.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпреЗ) (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рджрд┐рд╡рд┐) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд▓реЛрдХреЗ (рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢) рджрд╢ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдЪ (рд╕реНрде) рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдореН) рднреВрдореМ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ (рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢) (рд╕реНрде) (рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдГ) рдпреЗрд╜рдкреНрд╕реБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ (рдорд╣рд┐рдирд╛) рдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдирд╛ (рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢) рджрд╢реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдордирд╢реНрдЪреЗрддрд┐ (рд╕реНрде) (рддреЗ) (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рд╕рдВрдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН (рдЗрдордореН) (рдЬреБрд╖рдзреНрд╡рдореН) рд╕реЗрд╡рдзреНрд╡рдореН рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╣реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреМ рдпреЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд▓реЛрдХреЗ рд╕рдиреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рджреНрдпреЗрд╜рдиреНрдпрддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдиреНрдд рдд рдПрд╡рд╛рд╜рддреНрд░ рдпрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рддреНрд░ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╡рдиреНрдд рдПрд╡ рддрддреНрд░ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН рдпрдерд╛рд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрдпреЛрдЧрдХреНрд╖реЗрдордГ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рее резрез реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╢реАрд▓рд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ рдмреЛрдзреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХреЛрдирдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧреЛ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреАрдд рдЬреЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдд рдЖрд╣реЗрдд рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЬреЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрд░ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд рддреЗрдЪ рдпреЗрдереЗ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рдЬрд┐рддрдХреЗ рдпреЗрдереЗ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд рддрд┐рддрдХреЗ рдЗрддрд░ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдд (рдЧреЛрд▓рд╛рдд) рд╣реА рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдпрдерд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЬрд╛рдгреВрди рдШреЗрдКрди рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рдпреЛрдЧрдХреНрд╖реЗрдо рдЪрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рд▓рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрез рее
